			<div id="b.GEN" type="book">
				<div id="b.GEN.1" type="chapter">
					<seg id="b.GEN.1.1" type="verse">
						In the beginning God created the heaven and the earth.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.1.2" type="verse">
						And the earth was without form, and void; and darkness was upon the face of the deep. And the Spirit of God moved upon the face of the waters.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.1.3" type="verse">
						And God said, Let there be light: and there was light.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.1.4" type="verse">
						And God saw the light, that it was good: and God divided the light from the darkness.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.1.5" type="verse">
						And God called the light Day, and the darkness he called Night. And the evening and the morning were the first day.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.1.6" type="verse">
						And God said, Let there be a firmament in the midst of the waters, and let it divide the waters from the waters.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.1.7" type="verse">
						And God made the firmament, and divided the waters which were under the firmament from the waters which were above the firmament: and it was so.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.1.8" type="verse">
						And God called the firmament Heaven. And the evening and the morning were the second day.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.1.9" type="verse">
						And God said, Let the waters under the heaven be gathered together unto one place, and let the dry land appear: and it was so.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.1.10" type="verse">
						And God called the dry land Earth; and the gathering together of the waters called he Seas: and God saw that it was good.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.1.11" type="verse">
						And God said, Let the earth bring forth grass, the herb yielding seed, and the fruit tree yielding fruit after his kind, whose seed is in itself, upon the earth: and it was so.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.1.12" type="verse">
						And the earth brought forth grass, and herb yielding seed after his kind, and the tree yielding fruit, whose seed was in itself, after his kind: and God saw that it was good.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.1.13" type="verse">
						And the evening and the morning were the third day.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.1.14" type="verse">
						And God said, Let there be lights in the firmament of the heaven to divide the day from the night; and let them be for signs, and for seasons, and for days, and years:
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.1.15" type="verse">
						And let them be for lights in the firmament of the heaven to give light upon the earth: and it was so.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.1.16" type="verse">
						And God made two great lights; the greater light to rule the day, and the lesser light to rule the night: he made the stars also.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.1.17" type="verse">
						And God set them in the firmament of the heaven to give light upon the earth,
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.1.18" type="verse">
						And to rule over the day and over the night, and to divide the light from the darkness: and God saw that it was good.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.1.19" type="verse">
						And the evening and the morning were the fourth day.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.1.20" type="verse">
						And God said, Let the waters bring forth abundantly the moving creature that hath life, and fowl that may fly above the earth in the open firmament of heaven.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.1.21" type="verse">
						And God created great whales, and every living creature that moveth, which the waters brought forth abundantly, after their kind, and every winged fowl after his kind: and God saw that it was good.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.1.22" type="verse">
						And God blessed them, saying, Be fruitful, and multiply, and fill the waters in the seas, and let fowl multiply in the earth.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.1.23" type="verse">
						And the evening and the morning were the fifth day.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.1.24" type="verse">
						And God said, Let the earth bring forth the living creature after his kind, cattle, and creeping thing, and beast of the earth after his kind: and it was so.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.1.25" type="verse">
						And God made the beast of the earth after his kind, and cattle after their kind, and every thing that creepeth upon the earth after his kind: and God saw that it was good.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.1.26" type="verse">
						And God said, Let us make man in our image, after our likeness: and let them have dominion over the fish of the sea, and over the fowl of the air, and over the cattle, and over all the earth, and over every creeping thing that creepeth upon the earth.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.1.27" type="verse">
						So God created man in his own image, in the image of God created he him; male and female created he them.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.1.28" type="verse">
						And God blessed them, and God said unto them, Be fruitful, and multiply, and replenish the earth, and subdue it: and have dominion over the fish of the sea, and over the fowl of the air, and over every living thing that moveth upon the earth.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.1.29" type="verse">
						And God said, Behold, I have given you every herb bearing seed, which is upon the face of all the earth, and every tree, in the which is the fruit of a tree yielding seed; to you it shall be for meat.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.1.30" type="verse">
						And to every beast of the earth, and to every fowl of the air, and to every thing that creepeth upon the earth, wherein there is life, I have given every green herb for meat: and it was so.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.1.31" type="verse">
						And God saw every thing that he had made, and, behold, it was very good. And the evening and the morning were the sixth day.
					</seg>
				</div>
				<div id="b.GEN.2" type="chapter">
					<seg id="b.GEN.2.1" type="verse">
						Thus the heavens and the earth were finished, and all the host of them.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.2.2" type="verse">
						And on the seventh day God ended his work which he had made; and he rested on the seventh day from all his work which he had made.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.2.3" type="verse">
						And God blessed the seventh day, and sanctified it: because that in it he had rested from all his work which God created and made.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.2.4" type="verse">
						These are the generations of the heavens and of the earth when they were created, in the day that the LORD God made the earth and the heavens,
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.2.5" type="verse">
						And every plant of the field before it was in the earth, and every herb of the field before it grew: for the LORD God had not caused it to rain upon the earth, and there was not a man to till the ground.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.2.6" type="verse">
						But there went up a mist from the earth, and watered the whole face of the ground.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.2.7" type="verse">
						And the LORD God formed man of the dust of the ground, and breathed into his nostrils the breath of life; and man became a living soul.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.2.8" type="verse">
						And the LORD God planted a garden eastward in Eden; and there he put the man whom he had formed.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.2.9" type="verse">
						And out of the ground made the LORD God to grow every tree that is pleasant to the sight, and good for food; the tree of life also in the midst of the garden, and the tree of knowledge of good and evil.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.2.10" type="verse">
						And a river went out of Eden to water the garden; and from thence it was parted, and became into four heads.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.2.11" type="verse">
						The name of the first is Pison: that is it which compasseth the whole land of Havilah, where there is gold;
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.2.12" type="verse">
						And the gold of that land is good: there is bdellium and the onyx stone.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.2.13" type="verse">
						And the name of the second river is Gihon: the same is it that compasseth the whole land of Ethiopia.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.2.14" type="verse">
						And the name of the third river is Hiddekel: that is it which goeth toward the east of Assyria. And the fourth river is Euphrates.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.2.15" type="verse">
						And the LORD God took the man, and put him into the garden of Eden to dress it and to keep it.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.2.16" type="verse">
						And the LORD God commanded the man, saying, Of every tree of the garden thou mayest freely eat:
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.2.17" type="verse">
						But of the tree of the knowledge of good and evil, thou shalt not eat of it: for in the day that thou eatest thereof thou shalt surely die.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.2.18" type="verse">
						And the LORD God said, It is not good that the man should be alone; I will make him an help meet for him.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.2.19" type="verse">
						And out of the ground the LORD God formed every beast of the field, and every fowl of the air; and brought them unto Adam to see what he would call them: and whatsoever Adam called every living creature, that was the name thereof.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.2.20" type="verse">
						And Adam gave names to all cattle, and to the fowl of the air, and to every beast of the field; but for Adam there was not found an help meet for him.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.2.21" type="verse">
						And the LORD God caused a deep sleep to fall upon Adam and he slept: and he took one of his ribs, and closed up the flesh instead thereof;
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.2.22" type="verse">
						And the rib, which the LORD God had taken from man, made he a woman, and brought her unto the man.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.2.23" type="verse">
						And Adam said, This is now bone of my bones, and flesh of my flesh: she shall be called Woman, because she was taken out of Man.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.2.24" type="verse">
						Therefore shall a man leave his father and his mother, and shall cleave unto his wife: and they shall be one flesh.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.2.25" type="verse">
						And they were both naked, the man and his wife, and were not ashamed.
					</seg>
				</div>
				<div id="b.GEN.3" type="chapter">
					<seg id="b.GEN.3.1" type="verse">
						Now the serpent was more subtil than any beast of the field which the LORD God had made. And he said unto the woman, Yea, hath God said, Ye shall not eat of every tree of the garden?
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.3.2" type="verse">
						And the woman said unto the serpent, We may eat of the fruit of the trees of the garden:
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.3.3" type="verse">
						But of the fruit of the tree which is in the midst of the garden, God hath said, Ye shall not eat of it, neither shall ye touch it, lest ye die.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.3.4" type="verse">
						And the serpent said unto the woman, Ye shall not surely die:
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.3.5" type="verse">
						For God doth know that in the day ye eat thereof, then your eyes shall be opened, and ye shall be as gods, knowing good and evil.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.3.6" type="verse">
						And when the woman saw that the tree was good for food, and that it was pleasant to the eyes, and a tree to be desired to make one wise, she took of the fruit thereof, and did eat, and gave also unto her husband with her; and he did eat.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.3.7" type="verse">
						And the eyes of them both were opened, and they knew that they were naked; and they sewed fig leaves together, and made themselves aprons.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.3.8" type="verse">
						And they heard the voice of the LORD God walking in the garden in the cool of the day: and Adam and his wife hid themselves from the presence of the LORD God amongst the trees of the garden.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.3.9" type="verse">
						And the LORD God called unto Adam, and said unto him, Where art thou?
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.3.10" type="verse">
						And he said, I heard thy voice in the garden, and I was afraid, because I was naked; and I hid myself.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.3.11" type="verse">
						And he said, Who told thee that thou wast naked? Hast thou eaten of the tree, whereof I commanded thee that thou shouldest not eat?
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.3.12" type="verse">
						And the man said, The woman whom thou gavest to be with me, she gave me of the tree, and I did eat.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.3.13" type="verse">
						And the LORD God said unto the woman, What is this that thou hast done? And the woman said, The serpent beguiled me, and I did eat.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.3.14" type="verse">
						And the LORD God said unto the serpent, Because thou hast done this, thou art cursed above all cattle, and above every beast of the field; upon thy belly shalt thou go, and dust shalt thou eat all the days of thy life:
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.3.15" type="verse">
						And I will put enmity between thee and the woman, and between thy seed and her seed; it shall bruise thy head, and thou shalt bruise his heel.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.3.16" type="verse">
						Unto the woman he said, I will greatly multiply thy sorrow and thy conception; in sorrow thou shalt bring forth children; and thy desire shall be to thy husband, and he shall rule over thee.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.3.17" type="verse">
						And unto Adam he said, Because thou hast hearkened unto the voice of thy wife, and hast eaten of the tree, of which I commanded thee, saying, Thou shalt not eat of it: cursed is the ground for thy sake; in sorrow shalt thou eat of it all the days of thy life;
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.3.18" type="verse">
						Thorns also and thistles shall it bring forth to thee; and thou shalt eat the herb of the field;
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.3.19" type="verse">
						In the sweat of thy face shalt thou eat bread, till thou return unto the ground; for out of it wast thou taken: for dust thou art, and unto dust shalt thou return.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.3.20" type="verse">
						And Adam called his wife's name Eve; because she was the mother of all living.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.3.21" type="verse">
						Unto Adam also and to his wife did the LORD God make coats of skins, and clothed them.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.3.22" type="verse">
						And the LORD God said, Behold, the man is become as one of us, to know good and evil: and now, lest he put forth his hand, and take also of the tree of life, and eat, and live for ever:
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.3.23" type="verse">
						Therefore the LORD God sent him forth from the garden of Eden, to till the ground from whence he was taken.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.3.24" type="verse">
						So he drove out the man; and he placed at the east of the garden of Eden Cherubims, and a flaming sword which turned every way, to keep the way of the tree of life.
					</seg>
				</div>
				<div id="b.GEN.4" type="chapter">
					<seg id="b.GEN.4.1" type="verse">
						And Adam knew Eve his wife; and she conceived, and bare Cain, and said, I have gotten a man from the LORD.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.4.2" type="verse">
						And she again bare his brother Abel. And Abel was a keeper of sheep, but Cain was a tiller of the ground.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.4.3" type="verse">
						And in process of time it came to pass, that Cain brought of the fruit of the ground an offering unto the LORD.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.4.4" type="verse">
						And Abel, he also brought of the firstlings of his flock and of the fat thereof. And the LORD had respect unto Abel and to his offering:
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.4.5" type="verse">
						But unto Cain and to his offering he had not respect. And Cain was very wroth, and his countenance fell.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.4.6" type="verse">
						And the LORD said unto Cain, Why art thou wroth? and why is thy countenance fallen?
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.4.7" type="verse">
						If thou doest well, shalt thou not be accepted? and if thou doest not well, sin lieth at the door. And unto thee shall be his desire, and thou shalt rule over him.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.4.8" type="verse">
						And Cain talked with Abel his brother: and it came to pass, when they were in the field, that Cain rose up against Abel his brother, and slew him.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.4.9" type="verse">
						And the LORD said unto Cain, Where is Abel thy brother? And he said, I know not: Am I my brother's keeper?
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.4.10" type="verse">
						And he said, What hast thou done? the voice of thy brother's blood crieth unto me from the ground.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.4.11" type="verse">
						And now art thou cursed from the earth, which hath opened her mouth to receive thy brother's blood from thy hand;
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.4.12" type="verse">
						When thou tillest the ground, it shall not henceforth yield unto thee her strength; a fugitive and a vagabond shalt thou be in the earth.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.4.13" type="verse">
						And Cain said unto the LORD, My punishment is greater than I can bear.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.4.14" type="verse">
						Behold, thou hast driven me out this day from the face of the earth; and from thy face shall I be hid; and I shall be a fugitive and a vagabond in the earth; and it shall come to pass, that every one that findeth me shall slay me.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.4.15" type="verse">
						And the LORD said unto him, Therefore whosoever slayeth Cain, vengeance shall be taken on him sevenfold. And the LORD set a mark upon Cain, lest any finding him should kill him.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.4.16" type="verse">
						And Cain went out from the presence of the LORD, and dwelt in the land of Nod, on the east of Eden.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.4.17" type="verse">
						And Cain knew his wife; and she conceived, and bare Enoch: and he builded a city, and called the name of the city, after the name of his son, Enoch.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.4.18" type="verse">
						And unto Enoch was born Irad: and Irad begat Mehujael: and Mehujael begat Methusael: and Methusael begat Lamech.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.4.19" type="verse">
						And Lamech took unto him two wives: the name of the one was Adah, and the name of the other Zillah.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.4.20" type="verse">
						And Adah bare Jabal: he was the father of such as dwell in tents, and of such as have cattle.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.4.21" type="verse">
						And his brother's name was Jubal: he was the father of all such as handle the harp and organ.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.4.22" type="verse">
						And Zillah, she also bare Tubal-cain, an instructer of every artificer in brass and iron: and the sister of Tubal-cain was Naamah.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.4.23" type="verse">
						And Lamech said unto his wives, Adah and Zillah, Hear my voice; ye wives of Lamech, hearken unto my speech: for I have slain a man to my wounding, and a young man to my hurt.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.4.24" type="verse">
						If Cain shall be avenged sevenfold, truly Lamech seventy and sevenfold.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.4.25" type="verse">
						And Adam knew his wife again; and she bare a son, and called his name Seth: For God, said she, hath appointed me another seed instead of Abel, whom Cain slew.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.4.26" type="verse">
						And to Seth, to him also there was born a son; and he called his name Enos: then began men to call upon the name of the LORD.
					</seg>
				</div>
				<div id="b.GEN.5" type="chapter">
					<seg id="b.GEN.5.1" type="verse">
						This is the book of the generations of Adam. In the day that God created man, in the likeness of God made he him;
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.5.2" type="verse">
						Male and female created he them; and blessed them, and called their name Adam, in the day when they were created.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.5.3" type="verse">
						And Adam lived an hundred and thirty years, and begat a son in his own likeness, after his image; and called his name Seth:
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.5.4" type="verse">
						And the days of Adam after he had begotten Seth were eight hundred years: and he begat sons and daughters:
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.5.5" type="verse">
						And all the days that Adam lived were nine hundred and thirty years: and he died.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.5.6" type="verse">
						And Seth lived an hundred and five years, and begat Enos:
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.5.7" type="verse">
						And Seth lived after he begat Enos eight hundred and seven years, and begat sons and daughters:
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.5.8" type="verse">
						And all the days of Seth were nine hundred and twelve years: and he died.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.5.9" type="verse">
						And Enos lived ninety years, and begat Cainan:
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.5.10" type="verse">
						And Enos lived after he begat Cainan eight hundred and fifteen years, and begat sons and daughters:
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.5.11" type="verse">
						And all the days of Enos were nine hundred and five years: and he died.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.5.12" type="verse">
						And Cainan lived seventy years, and begat Mahalaleel:
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.5.13" type="verse">
						And Cainan lived after he begat Mahalaleel eight hundred and forty years, and begat sons and daughters:
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.5.14" type="verse">
						And all the days of Cainan were nine hundred and ten years: and he died.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.5.15" type="verse">
						And Mahalaleel lived sixty and five years, and begat Jared:
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.5.16" type="verse">

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.6.17" type="verse">

					</seg>

					</seg>

					</seg>

					</seg>

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.16.4" type="verse">

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.16.5" type="verse">
						And Sarai said unto Abram, My wrong be upon thee: I have given my maid into thy bosom; and when she saw that she had conceived, I was despised in her eyes: the LORD judge between me and thee.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.16.6" type="verse">
						But Abram said unto Sarai, Behold, thy maid is in thy hand; do to her as it pleaseth thee. And when Sarai dealt hardly with her, she fled from her face.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.16.7" type="verse">
						And the angel of the LORD found her by a fountain of water in the wilderness, by the fountain in the way to Shur.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.16.8" type="verse">
						And he said, Hagar, Sarai's maid, whence camest thou? and whither wilt thou go? And she said, I flee from the face of my mistress Sarai.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.16.9" type="verse">
						And the angel of the LORD said unto her, Return to thy mistress, and submit thyself under her hands.
					</seg>

					<seg id="b.GEN.16.12" type="verse">

				<div id="b.GEN.17" type="chapter">
					<seg id="b.GEN.17.1" type="verse">
						And when Abram was ninety years old and nine, the LORD appeared to Abram, and said unto him, I am the Almighty God; walk before me, and be thou perfect.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.17.2" type="verse">
						And I will make my covenant between me and thee, and will multiply thee exceedingly.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.17.3" type="verse">
						And Abram fell on his face: and God talked with him, saying,
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.17.4" type="verse">
						As for me, behold, my covenant is with thee, and thou shalt be a father of many nations.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.17.5" type="verse">
						Neither shall thy name any more be called Abram, but thy name shall be Abraham; for a father of many nations have I made thee.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.17.6" type="verse">
						And I will make thee exceeding fruitful, and I will make nations of thee, and kings shall come out of thee.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.17.7" type="verse">
						And I will establish my covenant between me and thee and thy seed after thee in their generations for an everlasting covenant, to be a God unto thee, and to thy seed after thee.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.17.8" type="verse">
						And I will give unto thee, and to thy seed after thee, the land wherein thou art a stranger, all the land of Canaan, for an everlasting possession; and I will be their God.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.17.9" type="verse">
						And God said unto Abraham, Thou shalt keep my covenant therefore, thou, and thy seed after thee in their generations.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.17.10" type="verse">
						This is my covenant, which ye shall keep, between me and you and thy seed after thee; Every man child among you shall be circumcised.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.17.11" type="verse">
						And ye shall circumcise the flesh of your foreskin; and it shall be a token of the covenant betwixt me and you.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.17.12" type="verse">
						And he that is eight days old shall be circumcised among you, every man child in your generations, he that is born in the house, or bought with money of any stranger, which is not of thy seed.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.17.13" type="verse">
						He that is born in thy house, and he that is bought with thy money, must needs be circumcised: and my covenant shall be in your flesh for an everlasting covenant.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.17.14" type="verse">
						And the uncircumcised man child whose flesh of his foreskin is not circumcised, that soul shall be cut off from his people; he hath broken my covenant.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.17.15" type="verse">
						And God said unto Abraham, As for Sarai thy wife, thou shalt not call her name Sarai, but Sarah shall her name be.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.17.16" type="verse">
						And I will bless her, and give thee a son also of her: yea, I will bless her, and she shall be a mother of nations; kings of people shall be of her.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.17.17" type="verse">
						Then Abraham fell upon his face, and laughed, and said in his heart, Shall a child be born unto him that is an hundred years old? and shall Sarah, that is ninety years old, bear?
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.17.18" type="verse">
						And Abraham said unto God, O that Ishmael might live before thee!
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.17.19" type="verse">
						And God said, Sarah thy wife shall bear thee a son indeed; and thou shalt call his name Isaac: and I will establish my covenant with him for an everlasting covenant, and with his seed after him.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.17.20" type="verse">

					</seg>

						But my covenant will I establish with Isaac, which Sarah shall bear unto thee at this set time in the next year.
					</seg>

						And he left off talking with him, and God went up from Abraham.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.17.23" type="verse">
						And Abraham took Ishmael his son, and all that were born in his house, and all that were bought with his money, every male among the men of Abraham's house; and circumcised the flesh of their foreskin in the selfsame day, as God had said unto him.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.17.24" type="verse">
						And Abraham was ninety years old and nine, when he was circumcised in the flesh of his foreskin.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.17.25" type="verse">
						And Ishmael his son was thirteen years old, when he was circumcised in the flesh of his foreskin.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.17.26" type="verse">

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.17.27" type="verse">

					</seg>

					</seg>

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.18.25" type="verse">

					</seg>

					</seg>

					</seg>

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.18.29" type="verse">

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.18.30" type="verse">
						And he said unto him, Oh let not the Lord be angry, and I will speak: Peradventure there shall thirty be found there. And he said, I will not do it, if I find thirty there.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.18.31" type="verse">

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.18.32" type="verse">

					</seg>

					</seg>

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.19.9" type="verse">

					</seg>

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.19.14" type="verse">

					</seg>

					</seg>

				<div id="b.GEN.20" type="chapter">

					<seg id="b.GEN.20.3" type="verse">

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.20.4" type="verse">
						But Abimelech had not come near her: and he said, Lord, wilt thou slay also a righteous nation?
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.20.5" type="verse">
						Said he not unto me, She is my sister? and she, even she herself said, He is my brother: in the integrity of my heart and innocency of my hands have I done this.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.20.6" type="verse">
						And God said unto him in a dream, Yea, I know that thou didst this in the integrity of thy heart; for I also withheld thee from sinning against me: therefore suffered I thee not to touch her.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.20.7" type="verse">

					</seg>

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.20.10" type="verse">

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.20.11" type="verse">
						And Abraham said, Because I thought, Surely the fear of God is not in this place; and they will slay me for my wife's sake.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.20.12" type="verse">

					<seg id="b.GEN.27.35" type="verse">

					<seg id="b.GEN.27.36" type="verse">

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.27.37" type="verse">

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.27.38" type="verse">

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.27.39" type="verse">

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.27.40" type="verse">

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.27.42" type="verse">

					</seg>

					</seg>

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.27.45" type="verse">

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.35.3" type="verse">
						And let us arise, and go up to Bethel; and I will make there an altar unto God, who answered me in the day of my distress, and was with me in the way which I went.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.35.4" type="verse">
						And they gave unto Jacob all the strange gods which were in their hand, and all their earrings which were in their ears; and Jacob hid them under the oak which was by Shechem.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.35.5" type="verse">
						And they journeyed: and the terror of God was upon the cities that were round about them, and they did not pursue after the sons of Jacob.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.35.6" type="verse">
						So Jacob came to Luz, which is in the land of Canaan, that is, Bethel, he and all the people that were with him.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.35.7" type="verse">
						And he built there an altar, and called the place El-beth-el: because there God appeared unto him, when he fled from the face of his brother.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.35.8" type="verse">
						But Deborah Rebekah's nurse died, and she was buried beneath Bethel under an oak: and the name of it was called Allon-bachuth.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.35.9" type="verse">
						And God appeared unto Jacob again, when he came out of Padan-aram, and blessed him.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.35.10" type="verse">
						And God said unto him, Thy name is Jacob: thy name shall not be called any more Jacob, but Israel shall be thy name: and he called his name Israel.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.35.11" type="verse">
						And God said unto him, I am God Almighty: be fruitful and multiply; a nation and a company of nations shall be of thee, and kings shall come out of thy loins;
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.35.12" type="verse">
						And the land which I gave Abraham and Isaac, to thee I will give it, and to thy seed after thee will I give the land.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.35.13" type="verse">
						And God went up from him in the place where he talked with him.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.35.14" type="verse">
						And Jacob set up a pillar in the place where he talked with him, even a pillar of stone: and he poured a drink offering thereon, and he poured oil thereon.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.35.15" type="verse">
						And Jacob called the name of the place where God spake with him, Bethel.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.35.16" type="verse">
						And they journeyed from Bethel; and there was but a little way to come to Ephrath: and Rachel travailed, and she had hard labour.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.35.17" type="verse">
						And it came to pass, when she was in hard labour, that the midwife said unto her, Fear not; thou shalt have this son also.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.35.18" type="verse">
						And it came to pass, as her soul was in departing, (for she died) that she called his name Ben-oni: but his father called him Benjamin.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.35.19" type="verse">
						And Rachel died, and was buried in the way to Ephrath, which is Bethlehem.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.35.20" type="verse">
						And Jacob set a pillar upon her grave: that is the pillar of Rachel's grave unto this day.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.35.21" type="verse">
						And Israel journeyed, and spread his tent beyond the tower of Edar.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.35.22" type="verse">
						And it came to pass, when Israel dwelt in that land, that Reuben went and lay with Bilhah his father's concubine: and Israel heard it. Now the sons of Jacob were twelve:
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.35.23" type="verse">
						The sons of Leah; Reuben, Jacob's firstborn, and Simeon, and Levi, and Judah, and Issachar, and Zebulun:
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.35.24" type="verse">
						The sons of Rachel; Joseph, and Benjamin:
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.35.25" type="verse">
						And the sons of Bilhah, Rachel's handmaid; Dan, and Naphtali:
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.35.26" type="verse">
						And the sons of Zilpah, Leah's handmaid; Gad, and Asher: these are the sons of Jacob, which were born to him in Padan-aram.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.35.27" type="verse">
						And Jacob came unto Isaac his father unto Mamre, unto the city of Arbah, which is Hebron, where Abraham and Isaac sojourned.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.35.28" type="verse">
						And the days of Isaac were an hundred and fourscore years.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.35.29" type="verse">
						And Isaac gave up the ghost, and died, and was gathered unto his people, being old and full of days: and his sons Esau and Jacob buried him.
					</seg>

					</seg>

					</seg>

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.36.5" type="verse">

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.36.6" type="verse">
						And Esau took his wives, and his sons, and his daughters, and all the persons of his house, and his cattle, and all his beasts, and all his substance, which he had got in the land of Canaan; and went into the country from the face of his brother Jacob.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.36.7" type="verse">

					</seg>

					</seg>

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.36.13" type="verse">

					</seg>

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.36.18" type="verse">

					</seg>

					</seg>

					</seg>

					</seg>

					</seg>

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.36.40" type="verse">

					</seg>

				<div id="b.GEN.37" type="chapter">
					<seg id="b.GEN.37.1" type="verse">
						And Jacob dwelt in the land wherein his father was a stranger, in the land of Canaan.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.37.2" type="verse">
						These are the generations of Jacob. Joseph, being seventeen years old, was feeding the flock with his brethren; and the lad was with the sons of Bilhah, and with the sons of Zilpah, his father's wives: and Joseph brought unto his father their evil report.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.37.3" type="verse">
						Now Israel loved Joseph more than all his children, because he was the son of his old age: and he made him a coat of many colours.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.37.4" type="verse">
						And when his brethren saw that their father loved him more than all his brethren, they hated him, and could not speak peaceably unto him.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.37.5" type="verse">
						And Joseph dreamed a dream, and he told it his brethren: and they hated him yet the more.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.37.6" type="verse">
						And he said unto them, Hear, I pray you, this dream which I have dreamed:
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.37.7" type="verse">
						For, behold, we were binding sheaves in the field, and, lo, my sheaf arose, and also stood upright; and, behold, your sheaves stood round about, and made obeisance to my sheaf.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.37.8" type="verse">
						And his brethren said to him, Shalt thou indeed reign over us? or shalt thou indeed have dominion over us? And they hated him yet the more for his dreams, and for his words.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.37.9" type="verse">
						And he dreamed yet another dream, and told it his brethren, and said, Behold, I have dreamed a dream more; and, behold, the sun and the moon and the eleven stars made obeisance to me.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.37.10" type="verse">
						And he told it to his father, and to his brethren: and his father rebuked him, and said unto him, What is this dream that thou hast dreamed? Shall I and thy mother and thy brethren indeed come to bow down ourselves to thee to the earth?
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.37.11" type="verse">
						And his brethren envied him; but his father observed the saying.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.37.12" type="verse">
						And his brethren went to feed their father's flock in Shechem.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.37.13" type="verse">
						And Israel said unto Joseph, Do not thy brethren feed the flock in Shechem? come, and I will send thee unto them. And he said to him, Here am I.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.37.14" type="verse">
						And he said to him, Go, I pray thee, see whether it be well with thy brethren, and well with the flocks; and bring me word again. So he sent him out of the vale of Hebron, and he came to Shechem.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.37.15" type="verse">
						And a certain man found him, and, behold, he was wandering in the field: and the man asked him, saying, What seekest thou?
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.37.16" type="verse">
						And he said, I seek my brethren: tell me, I pray thee, where they feed their flocks.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.37.17" type="verse">
						And the man said, They are departed hence; for I heard them say, Let us go to Dothan. And Joseph went after his brethren, and found them in Dothan.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.37.18" type="verse">
						And when they saw him afar off, even before he came near unto them, they conspired against him to slay him.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.37.19" type="verse">
						And they said one to another, Behold, this dreamer cometh.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.37.20" type="verse">
						Come now therefore, and let us slay him, and cast him into some pit, and we will say, Some evil beast hath devoured him: and we shall see what will become of his dreams.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.37.21" type="verse">
						And Reuben heard it, and he delivered him out of their hands; and said, Let us not kill him.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.37.22" type="verse">
						And Reuben said unto them, Shed no blood, but cast him into this pit that is in the wilderness, and lay no hand upon him; that he might rid him out of their hands, to deliver him to his father again.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.37.23" type="verse">
						And it came to pass, when Joseph was come unto his brethren, that they stript Joseph out of his coat, his coat of many colours that was on him;
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.37.24" type="verse">
						And they took him, and cast him into a pit: and the pit was empty, there was no water in it.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.37.25" type="verse">
						And they sat down to eat bread: and they lifted up their eyes and looked, and, behold, a company of Ishmeelites came from Gilead with their camels bearing spicery and balm and myrrh, going to carry it down to Egypt.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.37.26" type="verse">
						And Judah said unto his brethren, What profit is it if we slay our brother, and conceal his blood?
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.37.27" type="verse">
						Come, and let us sell him to the Ishmeelites, and let not our hand be upon him; for he is our brother and our flesh. And his brethren were content.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.37.28" type="verse">
						Then there passed by Midianites merchantmen; and they drew and lifted up Joseph out of the pit, and sold Joseph to the Ishmeelites for twenty pieces of silver: and they brought Joseph into Egypt.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.37.29" type="verse">
						And Reuben returned unto the pit; and, behold, Joseph was not in the pit; and he rent his clothes.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.37.30" type="verse">
						And he returned unto his brethren, and said, The child is not; and I, whither shall I go?
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.37.31" type="verse">
						And they took Joseph's coat, and killed a kid of the goats, and dipped the coat in the blood;
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.37.32" type="verse">
						And they sent the coat of many colours, and they brought it to their father; and said, This have we found: know now whether it be thy son's coat or no.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.37.33" type="verse">
						And he knew it, and said, It is my son's coat; an evil beast hath devoured him; Joseph is without doubt rent in pieces.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.37.34" type="verse">
						And Jacob rent his clothes, and put sackcloth upon his loins, and mourned for his son many days.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.37.35" type="verse">
						And all his sons and all his daughters rose up to comfort him; but he refused to be comforted; and he said, For I will go down into the grave unto my son mourning. Thus his father wept for him.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.37.36" type="verse">
						And the Midianites sold him into Egypt unto Potiphar, an officer of Pharaoh's, and captain of the guard.
					</seg>
				</div>
				<div id="b.GEN.38" type="chapter">
					<seg id="b.GEN.38.1" type="verse">
						And it came to pass at that time, that Judah went down from his brethren, and turned in to a certain Adullamite, whose name was Hirah.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.38.2" type="verse">
						And Judah saw there a daughter of a certain Canaanite, whose name was Shuah; and he took her, and went in unto her.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.38.3" type="verse">
						And she conceived, and bare a son; and he called his name Er.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.38.4" type="verse">
						And she conceived again, and bare a son; and she called his name Onan.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.38.5" type="verse">
						And she yet again conceived, and bare a son; and called his name Shelah: and he was at Chezib, when she bare him.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.38.6" type="verse">
						And Judah took a wife for Er his firstborn, whose name was Tamar.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.38.7" type="verse">
						And Er, Judah's firstborn, was wicked in the sight of the LORD; and the LORD slew him.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.38.8" type="verse">
						And Judah said unto Onan, Go in unto thy brother's wife, and marry her, and raise up seed to thy brother.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.38.9" type="verse">
						And Onan knew that the seed should not be his; and it came to pass, when he went in unto his brother's wife, that he spilled it on the ground, lest that he should give seed to his brother.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.38.10" type="verse">
						And the thing which he did displeased the LORD: wherefore he slew him also.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.38.11" type="verse">
						Then said Judah to Tamar his daughter in law, Remain a widow at thy father's house, till Shelah my son be grown: for he said, Lest peradventure he die also, as his brethren did. And Tamar went and dwelt in her father's house.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.38.12" type="verse">
						And in process of time the daughter of Shuah Judah's wife died; and Judah was comforted, and went up unto his sheepshearers to Timnath, he and his friend Hirah the Adullamite.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.38.13" type="verse">
						And it was told Tamar, saying, Behold thy father in law goeth up to Timnath to shear his sheep.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.38.14" type="verse">
						And she put her widow's garments off from her, and covered her with a vail, and wrapped herself, and sat in an open place, which is by the way to Timnath; for she saw that Shelah was grown, and she was not given unto him to wife.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.38.15" type="verse">
						When Judah saw her, he thought her to be an harlot; because she had covered her face.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.38.16" type="verse">
						And he turned unto her by the way, and said, Go to, I pray thee, let me come in unto thee; (for he knew not that she was his daughter in law.) And she said, What wilt thou give me, that thou mayest come in unto me?
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.38.17" type="verse">
						And he said, I will send thee a kid from the flock. And she said, Wilt thou give me a pledge, till thou send it?
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.38.18" type="verse">
						And he said, What pledge shall I give thee? And she said, Thy signet, and thy bracelets, and thy staff that is in thine hand. And he gave it her, and came in unto her, and she conceived by him.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.38.19" type="verse">
						And she arose, and went away, and laid by her vail from her, and put on the garments of her widowhood.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.38.20" type="verse">
						And Judah sent the kid by the hand of his friend the Adullamite, to receive his pledge from the woman's hand: but he found her not.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.38.21" type="verse">
						Then he asked the men of that place, saying, Where is the harlot, that was openly by the way side? And they said, There was no harlot in this place.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.38.22" type="verse">
						And he returned to Judah, and said, I cannot find her; and also the men of the place said, that there was no harlot in this place.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.38.23" type="verse">
						And Judah said, Let her take it to her, lest we be shamed: behold, I sent this kid, and thou hast not found her.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.38.24" type="verse">
						And it came to pass about three months after, that it was told Judah, saying, Tamar thy daughter in law hath played the harlot; and also, behold, she is with child by whoredom. And Judah said, Bring her forth, and let her be burnt.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.38.25" type="verse">

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.38.26" type="verse">

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.38.27" type="verse">
						And it came to pass in the time of her travail, that, behold, twins were in her womb.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.38.28" type="verse">
						And it came to pass, when she travailed, that the one put out his hand: and the midwife took and bound upon his hand a scarlet thread, saying, This came out first,
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.38.29" type="verse">
						And it came to pass, as he drew back his hand, that, behold, his brother came out: and she said, How hast thou broken forth? this breach be upon thee: therefore his name was called Pharez.
					</seg>

				<div id="b.GEN.39" type="chapter">
					<seg id="b.GEN.39.1" type="verse">
						And Joseph was brought down to Egypt; and Potiphar, an officer of Pharaoh, captain of the guard, an Egyptian, bought him of the hands of the Ishmeelites, which had brought him down thither.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.39.2" type="verse">
						And the LORD was with Joseph, and he was a prosperous man; and he was in the house of his master the Egyptian.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.39.3" type="verse">
						And his master saw that the LORD was with him, and that the LORD made all that he did to prosper in his hand.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.39.4" type="verse">

					<seg id="b.GEN.39.5" type="verse">
						And it came to pass from the time that he had made him overseer in his house, and over all that he had, that the LORD blessed the Egyptian's house for Joseph's sake; and the blessing of the LORD was upon all that he had in the house, and in the field.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.39.6" type="verse">
						And he left all that he had in Joseph's hand; and he knew not ought he had, save the bread which he did eat. And Joseph was a goodly person, and well favoured.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.39.7" type="verse">

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.39.8" type="verse">

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.39.9" type="verse">

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.39.10" type="verse">

					<seg id="b.GEN.39.11" type="verse">

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.39.12" type="verse">

					</seg>

					</seg>

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.39.15" type="verse">

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.39.16" type="verse">

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.39.17" type="verse">

					</seg>

					</seg>

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.40.6" type="verse">

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.40.9" type="verse">

					</seg>

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.40.11" type="verse">

					</seg>

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.40.13" type="verse">

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.40.14" type="verse">

					</seg>

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.40.16" type="verse">

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.40.17" type="verse">

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.40.18" type="verse">

					</seg>

				<div id="b.GEN.41" type="chapter">
					<seg id="b.GEN.41.1" type="verse">

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.41.2" type="verse">

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.41.3" type="verse">
						And, behold, seven other kine came up after them out of the river, ill favoured and leanfleshed; and stood by the other kine upon the brink of the river.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.41.4" type="verse">
						And the ill favoured and leanfleshed kine did eat up the seven well favoured and fat kine. So Pharaoh awoke.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.41.5" type="verse">
						And he slept and dreamed the second time: and, behold, seven ears of corn came up upon one stalk, rank and good.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.41.6" type="verse">
						And, behold, seven thin ears and blasted with the east wind sprung up after them.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.41.7" type="verse">
						And the seven thin ears devoured the seven rank and full ears. And Pharaoh awoke, and, behold, it was a dream.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.41.8" type="verse">
						And it came to pass in the morning that his spirit was troubled; and he sent and called for all the magicians of Egypt, and all the wise men thereof: and Pharaoh told them his dream; but there was none that could interpret them unto Pharaoh.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.41.9" type="verse">
						Then spake the chief butler unto Pharaoh, saying, I do remember my faults this day:
					</seg>

					</seg>

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.41.12" type="verse">

					</seg>

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.41.15" type="verse">
						And Pharaoh said unto Joseph, I have dreamed a dream, and there is none that can interpret it: and I have heard say of thee, that thou canst understand a dream to interpret it.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.41.16" type="verse">
						And Joseph answered Pharaoh, saying, It is not in me: God shall give Pharaoh an answer of peace.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.41.17" type="verse">
						And Pharaoh said unto Joseph, In my dream, behold, I stood upon the bank of the river:
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.41.18" type="verse">
						And, behold, there came up out of the river seven kine, fatfleshed and well favoured; and they fed in a meadow:
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.41.19" type="verse">
						And, behold, seven other kine came up after them, poor and very ill favoured and leanfleshed, such as I never saw in all the land of Egypt for badness:
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.41.20" type="verse">
						And the lean and the ill favoured kine did eat up the first seven fat kine:
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.41.21" type="verse">
						And when they had eaten them up, it could not be known that they had eaten them; but they were still ill favoured, as at the beginning. So I awoke.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.41.22" type="verse">
						And I saw in my dream, and, behold, seven ears came up in one stalk, full and good:
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.41.23" type="verse">
						And, behold, seven ears, withered, thin, and blasted with the east wind, sprung up after them:
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.41.24" type="verse">
						And the thin ears devoured the seven good ears: and I told this unto the magicians; but there was none that could declare it to me.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.41.25" type="verse">
						And Joseph said unto Pharaoh, The dream of Pharaoh is one: God hath shewed Pharaoh what he is about to do.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.41.26" type="verse">

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.41.27" type="verse">
						And the seven thin and ill favoured kine that came up after them are seven years; and the seven empty ears blasted with the east wind shall be seven years of famine.
					</seg>

					</seg>

					</seg>

					</seg>

					</seg>

					</seg>

					</seg>

					</seg>

				<div id="b.GEN.42" type="chapter">
					<seg id="b.GEN.42.1" type="verse">

					</seg>

					</seg>

					</seg>

					</seg>

					</seg>

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.42.7" type="verse">

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.42.8" type="verse">
						And Joseph knew his brethren, but they knew not him.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.42.9" type="verse">

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.42.10" type="verse">

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.42.11" type="verse">
						We are all one man's sons; we are true men, thy servants are no spies.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.42.12" type="verse">
						And he said unto them, Nay, but to see the nakedness of the land ye are come.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.42.13" type="verse">
						And they said, Thy servants are twelve brethren, the sons of one man in the land of Canaan; and, behold, the youngest is this day with our father, and one is not.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.42.14" type="verse">
						And Joseph said unto them, That is it that I spake unto you, saying, Ye are spies:
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.42.15" type="verse">
						Hereby ye shall be proved: By the life of Pharaoh ye shall not go forth hence, except your youngest brother come hither.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.42.16" type="verse">
						Send one of you, and let him fetch your brother, and ye shall be kept in prison, that your words may be proved, whether there be any truth in you: or else by the life of Pharaoh surely ye are spies.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.42.17" type="verse">
						And he put them all together into ward three days.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.42.18" type="verse">
						And Joseph said unto them the third day, This do, and live; for I fear God:
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.42.19" type="verse">
						If ye be true men, let one of your brethren be bound in the house of your prison: go ye, carry corn for the famine of your houses:
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.42.20" type="verse">
						But bring your youngest brother unto me; so shall your words be verified, and ye shall not die. And they did so.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.42.21" type="verse">
						And they said one to another, We are verily guilty concerning our brother, in that we saw the anguish of his soul, when he besought us, and we would not hear; therefore is this distress come upon us.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.42.22" type="verse">
						And Reuben answered them, saying, Spake I not unto you, saying, Do not sin against the child; and ye would not hear? therefore, behold, also his blood is required.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.42.23" type="verse">
						And they knew not that Joseph understood them; for he spake unto them by an interpreter.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.42.24" type="verse">
						And he turned himself about from them, and wept; and returned to them again, and communed with them, and took from them Simeon, and bound him before their eyes.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.42.25" type="verse">
						Then Joseph commanded to fill their sacks with corn, and to restore every man's money into his sack, and to give them provision for the way: and thus did he unto them.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.42.26" type="verse">
						And they laded their asses with the corn, and departed thence.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.42.27" type="verse">
						And as one of them opened his sack to give his ass provender in the inn, he espied his money; for, behold, it was in his sack's mouth.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.42.28" type="verse">
						And he said unto his brethren, My money is restored; and, lo, it is even in my sack: and their heart failed them, and they were afraid, saying one to another, What is this that God hath done unto us?
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.42.29" type="verse">
						And they came unto Jacob their father unto the land of Canaan, and told him all that befell unto them; saying,
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.42.30" type="verse">
						The man, who is the lord of the land, spake roughly to us, and took us for spies of the country.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.42.31" type="verse">
						And we said unto him, We are true men; we are no spies:
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.42.32" type="verse">
						We be twelve brethren, sons of our father; one is not, and the youngest is this day with our father in the land of Canaan.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.42.33" type="verse">
						And the man, the lord of the country, said unto us, Hereby shall I know that ye are true men; leave one of your brethren here with me, and take food for the famine of your households, and be gone:
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.42.34" type="verse">
						And bring your youngest brother unto me: then shall I know that ye are no spies, but that ye are true men: so will I deliver you your brother, and ye shall traffick in the land.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.42.35" type="verse">
						And it came to pass as they emptied their sacks, that, behold, every man's bundle of money was in his sack: and when both they and their father saw the bundles of money, they were afraid.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.42.36" type="verse">
						And Jacob their father said unto them, Me have ye bereaved of my children: Joseph is not, and Simeon is not, and ye will take Benjamin away: all these things are against me.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.42.37" type="verse">
						And Reuben spake unto his father, saying, Slay my two sons, if I bring him not to thee: deliver him into my hand, and I will bring him to thee again.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.42.38" type="verse">
						And he said, My son shall not go down with you; for his brother is dead, and he is left alone: if mischief befall him by the way in the which ye go, then shall ye bring down my gray hairs with sorrow to the grave.
					</seg>

					</seg>

				<div id="b.GEN.47" type="chapter">
					<seg id="b.GEN.47.1" type="verse">

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.47.5" type="verse">

					</seg>

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.47.10" type="verse">

					</seg>

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.47.13" type="verse">

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.47.14" type="verse">
						And Joseph gathered up all the money that was found in the land of Egypt, and in the land of Canaan, for the corn which they bought: and Joseph brought the money into Pharaoh's house.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.47.15" type="verse">
						And when money failed in the land of Egypt, and in the land of Canaan, all the Egyptians came unto Joseph, and said, Give us bread: for why should we die in thy presence? for the money faileth.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.47.16" type="verse">
						And Joseph said, Give your cattle; and I will give you for your cattle, if money fail.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.47.17" type="verse">
						And they brought their cattle unto Joseph: and Joseph gave them bread in exchange for horses, and for the flocks, and for the cattle of the herds, and for the asses: and he fed them with bread for all their cattle for that year.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.47.18" type="verse">
						When that year was ended, they came unto him the second year, and said unto him, We will not hide it from my lord, how that our money is spent; my lord also hath our herds of cattle; there is not ought left in the sight of my lord, but our bodies, and our lands:
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.47.19" type="verse">
						Wherefore shall we die before thine eyes, both we and our land? buy us and our land for bread, and we and our land will be servants unto Pharaoh: and give us seed, that we may live, and not die, that the land be not desolate.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.47.20" type="verse">
						And Joseph bought all the land of Egypt for Pharaoh; for the Egyptians sold every man his field, because the famine prevailed over them: so the land became Pharaoh's.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.47.21" type="verse">
						And as for the people, he removed them to cities from one end of the borders of Egypt even to the other end thereof.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.47.22" type="verse">

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.47.23" type="verse">
						Then Joseph said unto the people, Behold, I have bought you this day and your land for Pharaoh: lo, here is seed for you, and ye shall sow the land.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.47.24" type="verse">
						And it shall come to pass in the increase, that ye shall give the fifth part unto Pharaoh, and four parts shall be your own, for seed of the field, and for your food, and for them of your households, and for food for your little ones.
					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.47.25" type="verse">

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.47.26" type="verse">

					</seg>

					</seg>

					</seg>
					<seg id="b.GEN.47.30" type="verse">
